Excellent service by polite attentive staff. We had a large group, but disruptions were held to a minimum and everyone was served in timely fashion.  Excellent Old World Italian cuisine, with just a touch of home.  Fabulous sauces, excellent entrees, delightful antipasti and salads. This is one of the best Italian eateries I have ever been to, bar none.  Do yourself a favor, give yourself plenty of time and take a friend and/or loved one. You won't be sorry!
/edited for spelling</review>

<text>I will never, ever eat Basilico again.

We made confirmed reservations via Open Table for tonight at 7:00pm for four people.  It was confirmed by Basilico by text and by email.

We showed up precisely at 7:00pm and were told by a hostess that they didn't have a table available for us.  I said "we made a reservation a week ago and the restaurant confirmed it".  She said they didn't have a table for us.  I was obviously upset, as this was the first chance we'd had to see our door neighbors since both our house burned down last Oct.  We were then told they could seat us "downstairs".  Downstairs is an open, meeting room, with no ambience and felt like a barn.

Given no choice we reluctantly took the table.  Another hostess seated us and apologized, stating "she should have saved you a table".  She stated "you should call the owner".  Iasked for his name and phone number - - we never received it.  After we were seated the original hostess came down and asked if there was anything she could do.  I said "a complimentary round of drinks would be nice".  She said "I'll have to call the owner".  We never heard from her again and nothing was comped on the check.

It got worse.  As if they were trying to ignore or punish us, we didn't get water, bread or a server for 20 minutes.  I finally waived a busboy over and got water for us.  Then nothing.  I finally waived down a waiter serving another table and said "we have not seen a server, asked if we wanted a drink, we've been ignored".  He took our drink orders, later our appetizer order and finally our dinner order. The appetizers and dinner came and that's the last we saw of our server until we were finished.  We ordered dessert and coffee which came.  Then we couldn't find our waiter to get our check.  It took 15 minutes for him to bring us a check.

This is factually true.  I would not go to Basilico.  If you make a reservation be prepared for them to tell you they haven't saved you a table and offer to seat you "downstairs" in a bare hall-like room.

There are many far better places to eat where customers are valued and respected.<//text></record></dataset><record>

< Text>
We had a fantastic time dining at Sommâ€™s Kitchen run by the multitalented Ian. Conceptually the experience is a surprise tasting menu supercharged with trophy wines and liquors. This all takes place at a 12 seat curved bar where you can see Ian assemble each menu item. Ian slow prepares the items in advance using slow cooking, curing, sous vide, etc. and then finishes the dishes in front of you. The food is great but then he uses his sommelier background to pair wines and in our case bourbons with each course. And not just any wines or bourbons, Ian is looking to take the mystique out of the trophy or cult brands (like Bryant Family, Saxum, Sine Qua Non, Stagg) and happily pours these to get diner reactions. The result by the end of the night will leave you in a state of rapture and eager to plan your next visit.< /Text>

<user>104744470175121497189< /user>< Text>
I've been twice with my husband. First for our anniversary and again 6 weeks later to bring family last night. Ian and his staff are absolutely amazing and very welcoming. The food is inventive and delicious, but not stuffy. Ian's explanations of the food and wine are fascinating and down to earth. He is more than happy to try to accommodate allergies and preference (my husband isnt big on seafood). If you like good food and wine then hands down this is an experience that should not be missed whether you're visiting or a local like us. There's  no set menu to allow room for new experiments and to vary based on seasonal ingredients. Be sure to plan ahead as he books up!<//Text>

<rate>4<//rate>< Text>
Iâ€™m still on the fence on this one.  On one hand I had a great experience wine tasting.   Food was tasty but left me quite hungry.  Had to go eat a real meal afterwards.

Let me explain.

About a dozen of you sit around a long circular bar type counter.  Owner/chef assembles small dishes that he pairs with wine.   Food is not cooked in front of you and is fairly easy to pull off.  Chef claims to have worked at a Michelin restaurant but these are not fancy dishes.

We had appetizers like sliced meats and cheese.  Also a warm soup.   Then came a chunk of salmon and a bit of steak.   Each dish was quite good but did not quite make a meal.  And Iâ€™m a small guy who typically does not eat much.

Each dish, however, was paired with a wine.  Wine education and pairing is the real strength here.    We had two kinds of bubblies, whites and reds.   They all quite good and paired really well.   When your glass was empty he would pour some more.   So that part was quite nice.

The seating is a bit peculiar.  Some people get the good seats and get to see what he is doing and others sit on the sides and donâ€™t get much of his attention.  The people who came the latest (the ones we all had to wait for) got the best seats so not sure how that works.

Part of the way through another group enters and they sit in a back room.   Now they get part of the chefâ€™s attention too.

Overall it was a fun experience. There was plenty of good wine to drink, but donâ€™t expect a filling meal.  Would I go back?   Yah, likely, but Iâ€™d eat first.<//Text>

<user>106393227217104859547< /user><username>Tamara Scholtz< /username><Date>1521046594806< /Date>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
< Text>
I love walking into a new situation and not being exactly sure what I'm about to experience.  I love even more walking out thinking I can't WAIT to tell others that they need to experience this, too!

I think if people consider going to Somm's kitchen buying a ticket to an experience instead of paying a bill for dinner they'll get far more out of the ride.

On March 9, my husband and I were visiting Somm's kitchen from Austin, Texas.  We had been in Paso for the first time last year before this restaurant opened, so we were excited to try something new on the square.  We made a reservation about a month before.  When we walked in, Ian told us our spot was at the end of his semi circular bar which had enough room for about 14 people.

Ian greeted us and asked, "Are you hungry?"  We stated we were, and he handed us a glass of a most interesting Austrian sparkling wine.  We had no menu in front of us, wine or otherwise.  There was nothing to suggest what we might be eating, what we might be drinking, how many courses there may be, or even how much things might cost.

I'm sure we could have asked Ian, but we decided we were in for the ride!  For the next two hours we were in his hands as he had us try a local cheese, a foie gras that rivaled that of Michelin starred restaurants, a prime filet, lamb, and on and on...

It seemed some people came and went and didn't stay for the whole ride.  I'm not sure if all the kinks are ironed out there, but it didn't hinder our experience at all.

Each course was served with about a half of a glass of wine...unless of course you drank your wine, then more showed up.  None of the wines were particularly expensive, but all were particularly wonderful and the best paired I've ever had with any food ANYWHERE (and not to get all foodie/wine snobby... but we've been to Picasso, Cyrus, Robuchon... the pairing at Somm's Kitchen was simply AMAZING!)

The whole time we felt as though we were Ian's guests.  He chatted to us about the wines and the food and how he had prepared each thing.  At one point, he stopped and gave us a lesson in wine tasting.  It was taught in such a way that novice and experienced wine aficionados a like could enjoy. Ian is an experienced sommelier who teachers wine classes internationally, so getting a chance to experience this was quite a thrill!

In the French style, Ian prepared a salad between the final course and the desserts.  The salad was so creative.  He peeled the quail eggs and prepared it in front of us.  He carefully cut and placed herbs from right to left and as you ate, the herbs and the flavors increased in intensity with each bite.

We finished with desserts and feeling like we had made friends with our fellow diners and our host.

Our final bill was $250 for the two of us.  Both my husband and I felt this was truly a bargain.  We have paid more for less in the past.

Now, for the "to be completely honest" parts.  I would have liked a menu at least when we left if not to follow at the time.  Ian did say that I could email him and he would send a menu with all the information.  I intend to do that, but it would have been nice to look over it that evening, or even as I was writing this review.

Also, I'm not sure exactly how he decided who got what food.  There was a woman sitting next to me who I ran into twice again in the week while we were there.  Each time I saw her someplace else, she was telling other people that she was upset that she asked for potatoes and didn't get them even though some people did.  She did not like her experience at all and thought Ian was rude.  I thought he was funny and dry.  I liked his sense of humor, but I could see where others might find him off putting.  He's a New Yorker, not a Californian... and he still has some of the edge.

I also heard some complain about the price.   I think ANYWHERE you go 11 courses and 11 half glasses of wine for $125 a person is an amazing bargain... but I understand if you're thinking your'e only going to spend $50 on dinner.. this would be a little rough.</Text>

The Sledhill will be one of the best workouts of your life, and the most fun! We have been coming here for the last 15 years. Awesome place to learn some ski and snowboard moves. Everything can be rented, not allowed to bring your own sleds. Snow machine applies fresh layer for the slide Hill. Small kids snow play area is new and a great place for photos and kids to play without getting whacked in the head with a snowboard. They have a food truck and beers are available at their ticket window.< /review>

< Review>
tl;dr this place is great for kids of all ages and is worth the visit.

We came to this place on a whim and do not regret it. The location is a little tucked away, which may, or may not, be a good thing. Once you arrive there is plenty of parking. My family and I went sledding, and it was a blast. My kiddo was wiped out in no time because the sledding area requires all sledders to climb up a hill. There are two hill to choose from: 1. Main hill that picks up speed fast. I wouldn't recommend anyone under the age of 5 or 6 try this unless they are brave. 2. A smaller hill that is perfect for smaller children. There is also a skiing/snowboarding area; however, we didn't do that this time. I recommend this place!!< /Review>

< review>
Don't let the empty patio fool you, it's just cold outside. Tucked away indoors behind the taco joint is a magnificent eatery with Spanish rock pop establishing the ambience. From the moment we went over the house specials with server Alex to the moment the last drop of bottomless champagne was drained away, the service, the draft beer, and signature dishes did not disappoint. The titular Antigua seafood linguini was great, and so is the mango tuna tartar. The surf and turf was well balanced as well with the mushroom cream sauce to the perfectly medium rare Angus steak. Lastly, the lounging couch in the washroom corridor was also a nice touch. Would visit again.< /review>

< Text>
Good coffee spot that's probably way better when itt's not covid. The drinks were great but the atmosphere of the shop and the instagrammableness of the drinks are probably much more appealing than the flavors of the drinks themselves.

< text>
This place was aesthetically pleasing. I was really excited to try their blue latte based on pictures of other reviews. I ordered it with oat milk and even though it was really pretty to look at, taste wise it disappointed me. The taste was really bland and not worth my money. Beware this drink is non-caffeniated so that is also another strike for me. I would have rated this place higher if it wasn't for the owner's sarcasm. My order had already been placed and he approached us asking if we were from Pasadena etc. As we were talking I noticed they had stamp cards at my reach, which are usually offered to the customer when they make a purchase. I simply asked if he could stamp a card so I could come back and he replied very rude "No" in a very sassy way....I was shocked and replied why not? In my head I thought am I missing something? It took him a few seconds for him to say "I mean I could have refused you know?" Then he went on saying imagine if I had refused? And I understood he was probably joking but I don't understand why an owner of a new small business would joke around like that with new customers on their first interaction with the place....I could have definitely felt very offended and ask for my money back. Which I didn't but that's the reason I won't be returning to this place. Even aside from the whole owner to customer interaction, the taste of the latte is not worth me going back. I would much rather go to other coffee places like Jameson Brown  Coffee Roasters or Copa Vida their lattes are perfection.</text>

<resp>None</resp><user_name>Grace Wright<//user_name><Pictures>None</Pictures><user_id>101158630463675346359<//user_id><Rating>1< /Rating>< Text>
It's a shame "zero stars" isn't an option. My experience with U-Haul Moving & Storage of West Lancaster has been the single most infuriating customer "service" interaction I have ever had. The story begins when my U-Box was moved here when there was not enough room in Pasadena, where it was supposed to be stored. When I tried to call up to U-Haul Moving & Storage of West Lancaster and arrange to get my box returned to me, I could never get through to anyone actually in Lancaster; I would inevitably wait on hold for quite some time and then get rerouted to a corporate customer service line. Day after day I was assured that someone would return my call; it didn't happen. Finally, after 9 days of calling every day, I did get through to someone actually in Lancaster and was told that out of county delivery of my box would mean a nearly $500 charge - even though I had never wanted my things to be stored up there in the first place! After TWENTY-FOUR more phone calls over the next three days with various customer service agents, someone gave me the cell phone number of Chad Farren, the president of U Haul of San Fernando, who immediately arranged for it to be delivered to me - free of charge, but thanks to the incompetence of the individuals at U-Haul Moving & Storage of West Lancaster, nearly two weeks after I had needed it delivered.

So, I got my things, but the nightmare doesn't end here! U-Haul Moving & Storage of West Lancaster has continued to charge me for a storage space at their facility despite my having retrieved my things a month ago. I called yesterday - after a long wait on hold, was rerouted to the corporate customer service line, per usual - spoke to two agents and their manager, who could find no record of my contract and had no idea why I was still being charged, but said they eventually got through to the manager of U-Haul Moving & Storage of West Lancaster (Vanessa Ruiz, I assume) and sorted it out. I got an email refunding the last charge, and I was assured the account was closed out for good and I wouldn't be charged again and this whole nightmare would be over.

No surprise, it was not over!! I woke up this morning to another email saying I was charged again (!!!) for a month of storage, in the same amount that was refunded yesterday! At this point, I wonder whether I should even bother to call for what is probably the 40th time and try to get this refunded, or if I should just eat my losses and cancel my credit card to prevent future charges.

TL;DR you're better off just throwing any belongings you would store there straight into a landfill and trying to find them later, because digging through burning trash to recover your things would probably be a more pleasant experience than trying to deal with U-Haul Moving & Storage of West Lancaster. And it'll be less expensive.<//Text>

< Text>
In order to wash here you must purchase a card for 4 dollars, plus whatever money you need to wash. It must be exactly 4 dollars, and the dryers dont dry very good. The restrooms are clean, you need a quarter so make sure you get change if you know you'll be there a while. There are some vending machines, tables and chairs all the way to the left when you first enter. There is a door in that area that leads to the winchells next door. There is a little claw machine as well. Overall staff are attentive, and the place is clean. Just not the place for someone who only has a few bucks to dry.<//Text>
